British Ambassador Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen Presents Credentials to Chairman Lin; British Ambassador’s Address Expresses Sympathy for All of China's Construction; Chairman Lin Hosts a Banquet Attended by Ministers of Various Ministries

(Nanjing) British Ambassador Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen went to the National Government at 11:30 AM on the 23rd to meet Chairman Lin and present his credentials. Beforehand, at 11:00 AM, the National Government dispatched Tang Zhi, Director of the Protocol Department, and Liu Naifan, Section Chief, to go to the Ambassador's residence in Sa Jia Wan in government limousines to welcome him. The British Ambassador, accompanied by Counselor Hovell-Thurlow-Cumming-Bruce, Secretary Peter Comyn-Platt, Military Attaché Lieutenant-Colonel Gordon Lennox Temple Rorie, and seven attendants including Mr. Cholerton, traveled by car escorted by Tang and Liu and arrived at the government at 11:30 AM. The police along the way paid their respects. Two rows of guards and a band were lined up beside the driveway inside the gate of the National Government. As the Ambassador passed by, a salute was sounded and the national anthem of the Ambassador's country was played. Li Youchu, Chief of the Protocol Department, and Lin Tongshi, Chief of the External Affairs Section of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, welcomed him at the disembarkation point. Chief Aide-de-Camp Lü Chao welcomed him at the steps of the reception room and led the Ambassador into the room to rest. Then, the Director of the Protocol Department entered to announce that the Chairman was coming to the hall. The Chairman stood in the center, led by the Secretary-General Wei Huai and all the secretaries, and Chief Aide-de-Camp Lü Chao led all the aides-de-camp, standing on both sides. Minister of Foreign Affairs Zhang Qun and Duan Maolan, translator of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stood to the right of the Chairman. The Director of the Protocol Department invited the Ambassador to enter to meet the Chairman. After the Ambassador entered the hall and bowed to the Chairman according to etiquette, he began to deliver his address. After it was finished, the translator translated it into Chinese. After the translation, the Ambassador stepped forward to present his credentials. The Chairman received them and handed them to the Minister of Foreign Affairs, then recited his reply. After the translator finished translating, the Ambassador stepped forward, and the Chairman shook hands and talked with him. The translator stepped forward to convey the message. The Chairman first inquired about the health of the British Monarch. After a brief exchange, the Ambassador introduced the officials who had come with him, and the Chairman shook hands with each of them. The Ambassador retreated to his original position and bowed to the Chairman according to etiquette, and the Chairman returned the bows. The Ambassador and others exited the hall and were led into the reception room by the Director of the Protocol Department. The Minister of Foreign Affairs, the Secretary-General, and the Chief Aide-de-Camp entered the room at the same time and mingled with the Ambassador. The Chairman returned to his office to rest. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

(Nanjing) The translated text of British Ambassador Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen's address when presenting his credentials is as follows: "Your Excellency, Mr. Chairman, I, the Ambassador, have been appointed by His Majesty the King of my country as the Plenipotentiary Ambassador to China. I now present my credentials to Your Excellency and convey His Majesty the King of my country's sincere wishes for the prosperity of the Republic of China and admiration for Your Excellency. I am deeply honored to be appointed by His Majesty the King of my country to this close and important country at a time of great tension in the history of human evolution. Our two countries have always maintained friendly relations, and I sincerely wish to follow in the footsteps of previous ambassadors of my country to consolidate them. The success of your country's reconstruction efforts is highly regarded by the government and people of my country. I believe you are well aware of this. As Ambassador, I will adhere to this principle, sympathize with all of your country's future reconstruction efforts, and do my best to promote friendly understanding of your country by countries closely related to the Far East, so as to jointly achieve a realm of peace and prosperity." The original text of Chairman Lin's reply is as follows: "Your Excellency, Mr. Ambassador, I am very pleased to accept your credentials as the Plenipotentiary Ambassador of Great Britain to China, appointed by His Majesty the King of your country. I am particularly grateful for His Majesty the King of your country's friendly sentiments toward China and myself. I would like to take this opportunity to wish His Majesty the King of your country good health and the prosperity of his country in the name of the National Government and the people of China, and I hope you will convey this message. I am delighted to hear that the government and people of your country share a sense of goodwill toward China's reconstruction efforts, and that Your Excellency shares this sentiment and will do your best to promote friendly understanding of China by countries related to East Asia. I am deeply gratified by this, as it is essential that all countries in the world assist each other, as they always have, and especially now. Only in this way can we achieve the benefits of peace and prosperity. I am confident that if Your Excellency is determined to achieve this goal and works hard to the end, it will not only benefit China and Great Britain but also bring blessings to the world. Your Excellency has such a deep understanding of the national conditions of China, and the friendly relations between China and Great Britain will surely become even closer. The National Government and I will do our best to assist you so that you can fulfill your mission." (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

(Nanjing) At a tea party at his private residence in Gaoloumen on the afternoon of the 23rd, Kong Xiangxi, Vice President of the Executive Yuan, hosted the newly appointed British Ambassador Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen and his wife, and invited the ministers and councilors. After the banquet, the Director of the Protocol Department invited the Chairman, the Ambassador, and Secretary Hovell-Thurlow-Cumming-Bruce to take a photo in the corridor. Then, they went to the reception room for tea and cigarettes. The Chairman first shook hands with the Ambassador and said goodbye before returning to his office. The Ambassador also said goodbye and was escorted to the door of the reception room by Foreign Minister Zhang, to the bottom of the steps by the female official and the two chiefs aide-de-camp, and to the place where he boarded the car by the Section Chief of the Protocol Department and the External Affairs Section Chief of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The guards still paid their respects as before, and the band played the Chinese national anthem to see him off. The personnel sent to the embassy to welcome him were still taken by limousine back to the Ambassador's residence. After the British Ambassador returned to the residence, Chairman Lin sent his chief aide-de-camp with his card to return the visit. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

(Nanjing) Kong Xiangxi is scheduled to host a tea party at the ministry at 4:30 PM on the 24th to entertain the newly appointed British Ambassador to China, Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen, and to invite other foreign diplomats stationed in China and the heads of central ministries, committees, and councils. Rumors that Kong would go to Shanghai on the evening of the 23rd to be hospitalized for treatment are unfounded. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

(Nanjing) At 8 PM tonight, Foreign Minister Zhang hosted a banquet to welcome Ambassador Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen, with Vice Ministers Xu Mo and Chen Jie in attendance. Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen is scheduled to lead his staff to the Mausoleum on the morning of the 14th to lay flowers. In the afternoon at 4 PM, he will attend the tea party hosted by Minister Kong. In the evening, the Sino-British Cultural Association will host a banquet for Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen. The date of his trip north is expected to be sometime next week. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

Portugal Proposes Conditions for Participating in the Adjustment Committee; Foreign Minister of Spain Plans to Protest Neutrality Violations and Arms Supplies

(Geneva) After British Foreign Secretary Eden discussed with the Portuguese Foreign Minister this afternoon, British officials revealed that Portugal had accepted to participate in the Adjustment Committee for non-intervention in the Spanish civil war, but proposed multiple conditions. For example, since the Soviet Union is included in the Adjustment Committee, Portugal cannot allow the Adjustment Committee to have the power to control affairs within Portuguese territory.

(Lisbon) Regarding the issue of participating in the Adjustment Committee, there have been many rumors since Portugal proposed conditions. Prime Minister Salazar recently issued a statement to the newspapers, stating that Portugal will faithfully fulfill its obligations under the non-intervention agreement in the Spanish civil war. However, it is unwilling to give up all of its colonies and naval bases, and its foreign policy is not contrary to that of Great Britain. (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

(London) According to today's morning newspapers, the Spanish representative to the League of Nations, Foreign Minister Álvarez del Vayo, will send a note to the Great Powers in Geneva opposing Portugal's violation of neutrality. It is reported that the note will list the facts of Portugal's supply of arms to the Spanish rebels. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

The League of Nations Seeks to Restore Authority; Strives for Connections with the Americas; Tries to Harmonize Three International Conventions; Remarks by the President of the Assembly Reveal Clues; The Issue of Abyssinian Representation Is Put to the Vote at the Assembly

(Geneva) French Foreign Minister Delbos held talks with Argentine Foreign Minister Lamas (the current President of the League of Nations Assembly) today. Lamas declared that he is very willing to do his best to work to harmonize the Covenant of the League of Nations, the Saavedra Lamas Anti-War Treaty, and the Briand-Kellogg Pact. (Note: The Saavedra Lamas Anti-War Treaty, also known as the "Treaty on Non-Aggression and Conciliation Between American States," was initiated by Argentine Foreign Minister Saavedra Lamas and signed in the Argentine capital on October 10, 1933. The Briand-Kellogg Pact, also known as the Pact of Paris or the Kellogg-Briand Pact, was initiated by the late French Foreign Minister Briand and former US Secretary of State Kellogg and signed in Paris on August 27, 1928). In addition, Lamas said that Argentina hopes to develop economic and cultural relations with France and, through France's mediation, develop economic and cultural relations with European countries. Delbos replied that he expressed his deep sympathy for Lamas's plan and would do his best to seek closer ties between France and Argentina. (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

(Geneva) The Credentials Committee of the League of Nations Assembly held a closed meeting at 10:30 this morning to continue discussing the issue of Abyssinia's representative attending the Assembly. The chairman was Peruvian representative Tudela. The meeting adjourned at 1:05 PM and was scheduled to resume at 4:30 PM. It is generally believed that the committee will submit recommendations to the Assembly and allow it to choose freely. It is expected that the issue can be resolved when the Assembly meets at 6:30 PM this afternoon. Informed sources believe that if the Assembly decides to refer the case to the International Court of Justice in The Hague for a decision, Italy will definitely issue a statement that it will disregard all work of the League of Nations, but will not formally withdraw from the League of Nations at this time. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

Disarmament Negotiations; Possible Resumption in Geneva; Britain Is Willing to Voice Support for France

(Paris) When well-informed sources mentioned the possibility of resuming arms limitation negotiations in Geneva today, they all said that France did not want to submit a concrete disarmament plan to the League of Nations. The French government may issue a declaration on disarmament, but it will not contain concrete suggestions. This statement was made because the Paris correspondent of The Times of London had reported that disarmament negotiations might resume in Geneva. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

(London) According to well-informed sources, the British Cabinet Sub-Committee recently held a meeting chaired by Lord President of the Council MacDonald, with seven cabinet members in attendance. The following resolutions were passed: (1) To make the greatest possible effort to ensure that the Portuguese government participates in the work of the Adjustment Committee for non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War. (2) The Cabinet Sub-Committee decided that the British government should support France's efforts regarding arms reduction in Geneva. British cabinet members speculate that Germany's opposition to Britain and France on the issue of arms expansion is inevitable, which may be understood by German Head of State Hitler. (3) Regarding negotiations for convening a five-power Locarno conference, it was decided not to rush it, lest Germany demand the abolition of the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact. (4) To hear a report from Palestine regarding the recent Arab rebellion. (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

The Assembly Appoints Chairmen of Various Committees

(Geneva) The League of Nations Assembly elected the chairmen of various committees this afternoon. According to the practice of the League of Nations Assembly, seven committees are established. Among them, the Disarmament Committee has been suspended for years due to the holding of disarmament conferences. This year's Assembly has a proposal to re-establish the Disarmament Committee, but a final decision has not yet been made. As for the chairmen of the other six committees, they have been elected as follows: (1) Legal and Regulatory Committee: Chairman Limburg (Netherlands representative); (2) Technical Organization Committee: Chairman Langenhoven (Belgian representative); (3) Committee on Secretariat and Financial Questions: Chairman Guani (Uruguayan representative); (4) Disarmament Committee (vacant); (5) Social and Humanitarian Questions Committee: Chairman Schmidt (Estonian representative); (6) Political Questions Committee: Chairman Motta (Swiss representative); (7) Agenda Committee: Chairman Beck (Polish representative). (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

The Issue of Abyssinian Representation; Two Factions Confront Each Other in the League of Nations; The Great Powers Do Not Want to Displease Italy; The Small Countries Insist on Protecting the Rights of the Weak

(Geneva) The decision of the Credentials Committee of the League of Nations Assembly to refer the matter of Abyssinia's request to attend the Assembly to the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague for a decision may cause serious international disputes. Now, apart from Rome viewing this as an attempt to obstruct the harmony between Italy and the League of Nations, the representatives of the League of Nations will also be divided into two factions. The representatives of several great powers form one faction, known as the "realist faction." This faction said that Italy's withdrawal from the world radio conference was a warning, making it known that Abyssinia should be excluded from the League of Nations to avoid hindering the new European peace mechanism. The delegations of the small countries also form one faction, known as the "idealist faction." This faction firmly believes that the principle of protecting the rights of small countries is more important than Mussolini's cooperation with the League of Nations. At the same time, according to sources in Rome, the Italian government must wait until the League of Nations excludes Abyssinia before it plans to send a delegation to Geneva. The decision of the Credentials Committee greatly surprised Italy. Now, it is believed that Italy will refuse to participate in the Locarno Conference until the ruling of the Hague Tribunal on this issue is announced. If the ruling of the Hague Tribunal is unfavorable to Italy, it seems that Italy will no longer participate in any new Western European security agreement. The decision of the Credentials Committee will now be submitted to the Plenary Session of the League of Nations Assembly for a vote. Even this move has raised new questions: Whether recourse to the Hague Tribunal must be unanimously approved to be effective, or whether it can be effective with only a majority vote. If unanimous approval is necessary, this move may be difficult to achieve, because countries that have not imposed sanctions on Italy, such as Austria, Hungary, and Albania, will definitely vote against it. Even with this entanglement unresolved, another difficulty will arise: Whether Abyssinia's representatives should be suspended from attending the Assembly meetings while the Hague Tribunal has not made a decision. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Italy Withdraws from the Radio Conference; No Less Than a Warning to the League of Nations

(Geneva) The Italian delegation attending the International Radio Conference officially stated today that it did not want to continue participating in the work of the conference. Although the reasons it stated were purely technical, the general public in Geneva felt that the delegation's withdrawal from the conference was actually decided by Rome. This shows that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini is dissatisfied with the League of Nations Assembly's attitude toward Abyssinia. (Reuters dispatch, 22nd)

Legal Experts Draft a List of Questions; To Consult the Hague Tribunal

(Geneva) The League of Nations Assembly will only be able to decide on the issue of whether the Abyssinian delegation can continue to attend when it holds an open meeting tomorrow afternoon. At that time, the Credentials Committee attending will be able to submit a final report to the Assembly. Legal experts are now drafting a list of questions to ask the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague: Whether the Abyssinian Emperor can still send a delegation to represent Abyssinia at international conferences. As for the question of whether the Abyssinian delegation can continue to attend the League of Nations Assembly before the International Court of Justice makes a decision, it will be decided by a vote of the Assembly. The outcome of the vote will inevitably be that some will advocate attendance and some will oppose attendance. It is still too early to speculate on which faction will be in the majority. (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

All Roads Lead to One Place; Spanish Rebels Encircle the Capital; The Final Battle Begins at Any Moment; The Strategic Pass South of the Capital Was Occupied Yesterday

(Andai) Madrid is now almost surrounded by rebels, and a major battle is expected to begin within 24 hours. The government forces and rebels north of the capital are now digging trenches opposite each other on the peaks of the Guadarrama Mountains. However, in several places, the rebels have advanced to the Madrid area, threatening the headquarters of the government forces. The highway northeast to Zaragoza is now controlled by the rebels guarding Siguenza. The government forces south of the capital occupy Toledo, but they are hampered by the rebels in the Alcazar fortress, who are fighting to the death. The rebels in the fortress received a notice dropped by plane, stating that reinforcements would arrive within 48 hours. Therefore, although they were forced to withdraw from the stables and granaries in the fort, they are still hiding in underground caves, fighting hard to await the arrival of reinforcements. Only the southeast can be used by the government forces to transport military supplies and reinforcements. This road must pass through Albacete and Valencia. The rebel front in the southwest stretches from Torrijos (45 miles from Madrid) to Quismondo (5 miles from Maqueda), about 41 miles from the capital. After the government forces were defeated in Maqueda, they are now holding Quismondo. The town seems to be the focus of the rebels' general attack on the capital, because from there there is a wide motor road through flat land directly to the capital. The rebels in the west, northwest, and southwest have now joined together, but the mountain defenders are too thin, so the rebels are now almost surrounding their destination. However, a gap remains between Toledo and a point due east of Aranjuez. Aranjuez is located at a railway intersection and is now the only way out for the government forces. According to the rebel headquarters, there is now a strong force with a large number of aircraft gathered in the territory of Toledo, preparing to attack. The army will be commanded by General Varela, who has been overseeing the battle in the Malaga area until now. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

(Burgos) As a result of the rebels' occupation of the strategic town of Maqueda, 60 miles south of Madrid, yesterday, Madrid's position has fallen into a desperate situation. According to a senior rebel commander here, "Anything can happen now." Because the fall of Maqueda made the highway from the town to Ávila unobstructed, the rebels were able to advance to Toledo. Yesterday, the sound of artillery fire from the Alcazar fortress was incessant. After Prime Minister Caballero personally inspected the fortress, the artillery intensified its bombardment of the watchtower in the fort. However, by dusk, the watchtower still stood tall, so the government forces occupying a part of the fortress had no choice but to retreat. Before the fall of Maqueda, several rebel planes participated in a desperate battle and shelled the town fiercely. Three columns of rebels began to attack from the south, center, and north at dawn. Before the rebel planes destroyed the government defenses, the three columns were temporarily blocked by the mechanized government forces and could not advance. Before long, the shelling was successful, and the government militia lost their fighting spirit and boarded long-distance buses to retreat to Torrijos, 15 miles north of Toledo. The rebels, led by Moroccan troops, then occupied the town and pursued the victory. It is reported that the rebels killed thousands of militiamen in the battle. It is also reported that after the fall of Maqueda, there was a fierce battle between the planes of the rebels and the government forces at one time, but the government planes arrived too late to help the defenders. Soon, three rebel bomber planes flew over the city of Toledo and dropped bombs, destroying the important railway bridge in the Vargas area, connecting Madrid and Extremadura. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

The Mountain Pass Fell; The Government Forces Were Forced to Retreat

(Paris) A telegram received here from Talavera de la Reina said that as a result of the advance of the Spanish rebels in the Sierra de Gredos area, they have occupied the Puerto del Pico pass, and the highway to Ávila has been opened. It is reported that the government troops installed machine guns in the snow-covered Sierra de Gredos and even dragged cannons to the tops of two mountain peaks to control the small pass and the ancient Roman highway. Two rebel cavalry teams attacked the government troops stationed beside the mountain and defeated them. The government troops have retreated into the mountains. It is also reported that the government troops shot more than 500 people in the village of Arenas de San Pedro, including 15 young women, which accounted for almost one-tenth of the village's population. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

The Rebel Attack on the Northern Front of the Capital Was Frustrated

(Madrid) According to news from the Guadarrama Mountains front, the rebels suffered a major defeat in the battle near the Lozoya Reservoir, the main water supply source for the capital, and suffered heavy losses. The government troops have discovered more than 400 rebel soldiers' corpses, all of whom were killed while trying to break through the Madrid northwestern front. The intensity of this offensive was unprecedented, continuing day and night. Although the rebels had approached the government trenches and could launch hand grenades, they were taken advantage of by the government forces due to the darkness and suffered heavy losses before retreating, abandoning a lot of military materials. The government forces took advantage of the victory to pursue to a place two miles away before stopping. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Spain Calls Up Draftees

(Madrid) The national government radio station today broadcast an order calling up draftees across the country to organize a militia army. The Ministry of the Army announced that the new army will receive formal training. (National Telegram, 22nd)

Government Discovers Private Arms Smuggling; Nationwide Strict Investigation Launched

(Beijing) Today, the Belgian government has appointed a subcommittee composed of various administrative departments to investigate a conspiracy in which a certain Belgian party or parties provided a large quantity of arms to Spain. It is reported that the discovery of this case was due to the seizure of a suitcase on a train containing detailed plans regarding this matter, and it was also discovered that the center of this arms smuggling operation was the Antwerp area. Currently, the police are continuing to carry out investigations everywhere. It is reported that a large number of machine guns have been seized in the Waasland region. (Reuters, 23rd)

Uruguay Severs Diplomatic Relations with the Spanish Government; Extremely Indignant at the Execution of the Deputy Consul in the Capital of Spain; Entrusts Argentina to Handle Consular Protection Matters

Capital of Uruguay. The government of the Republic of Uruguay, due to the recent chaos in Spain during which its deputy consul stationed in Madrid and three nuns of the country were executed by the government forces, has decided to sever diplomatic relations with the Spanish government. Today, the President issued an order deciding: (1) to close the Uruguayan embassy in Spain and withdraw its diplomatic representatives stationed in Spain until the Spanish government provides full security guarantees to the diplomatic representatives and missionaries of other countries; (2) to order the Uruguayan chargé d'affaires in Spain to lodge a protest with the Spanish government through the Ministry of Foreign Affairs; (3) to request the Argentine government to handle the protection of Uruguayan nationals in Spain; (4) to forward the above orders to the League of Nations for record. As for whether the Uruguayan government will recognize the National Defense Military Government of Burgos as the legitimate government of Spain, it is still unknown. (Havas, 22nd)

Capital of Argentina. Since the outbreak of civil strife in Spain, the losses suffered by the nationals of South American countries residing there have already been considerable. After the news spread that the Uruguayan deputy consul in Madrid and three nuns had been executed by the Spanish government forces, public opinion here, in Uruguay, and in other South American countries was greatly shocked. The Spanish ambassador to Uruguay, Soriano, has resigned to his post and has claimed to be a diplomatic representative of the National Army government of Burgos. (Havas, 22nd)

Small Island in the South Pacific Integrated into the British Territory

Sydney. Since the accession of King Edward VIII, territory has been newly added for the first time today. This new territory has been formally received by four members of the Sydney Yacht Club. It is a small island located near the Elizabeth Reef in the South Pacific, 500 miles northeast of Sydney. It is also a coral reef, only ten feet above sea level, and has not yet been drawn into maps. (Guo Ri Dian, 22nd)

German Youth Group Parades in Front of the Palazzo Venezia; Received in Review by the Italian Prime Minister; Will Also Travel to Portugal

(Rome) The leader of the German National Socialist Youth Group, Shirach, recently led 500 members to Italy for a tour. This morning, after the members of the German Youth Group laid a wreath at the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier here, all the members lined up and paraded in front of the Palazzo Venezia. There was a huge crowd of spectators. Prime Minister Mussolini reviewed them from the balcony of the palace. Swedish Cabinet Resigns

Capital of Sweden. The cabinet has resigned en masse. The King has issued an order to the Social Democratic leader Hansson to form a cabinet. Hansson immediately expressed his acceptance. (Havas, 23rd)

U.S. Chargé d'Affaires in Japan Stabbed by Thief

(Tokyo) At around 5:00 AM on the 23rd, a thief, around 30 years old and dressed in worker's clothing, broke into the residence of American Embassy Chargé d'Affaires D'Ecaubay in Azabu district, Nakamachi, and was stealing items on the second floor. Mr. D'Ecaubay, hearing the noise, immediately stepped forward to arrest him. The thief pulled out a short knife and stabbed Mr. D'Ecaubay in the left arm, the wound reaching up to ten centimeters and penetrating to the periosteum. The thief then fled without taking anything. The Metropolitan Police Department is currently dispatching officers to search for the perpetrator. (Domei, 23rd)

(Tokyo) First Secretary and Chargé d'Affaires of the U.S. Embassy in Japan, Dickson Woofard, this morning was stabbed in the upper right arm while trying to apprehend a thief who had broken into his residence. Although he lost a lot of blood, his injuries are not life-threatening. It is expected that he will recover in about two weeks. As for the thief, he escaped and has not yet been caught. It is reported that the thief is likely a Japanese. He broke into Mr. Dickson's residence before dawn. When he broke into Mrs. Dickson's bedroom, she woke up and shouted for a thief. Mr. Dickson, hearing the sound, rushed over and tried to capture the thief, but was unexpectedly stabbed by him. Afterwards, personnel from the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs went to Mr. Dickson's residence to inquire about his injuries and expressed regret on behalf of the Japanese government. The personnel also said that the Japanese authorities will do their best to apprehend the culprit. It is reported that the incident does not have any political significance. (Reuters, 23rd)

Page 8

Lansing Memoirs: Japan Plans to Refute

(Tokyo) During the First World War, U.S. Secretary of State Lansing concluded the Ishii-Lansing Agreement with Japan's Ishii. Therefore, Lansing's posthumous manuscript, "Lansing's War Memoirs," was publicly sold by Merrill Publishing House this spring. The contents describe the famous Zimmermann Telegram leak incident, and the bold exposure of major international political secrets during the greatest crisis of the time caused a great stir around the world. Those parts concerning Japan are full of malicious criticism, stating that Japan's participation in the war was intended for aggression. This is not only a major insult to Japan, but also, without the understanding of the Japanese government, the secret diplomatic documents exchanged between Japan and the United States regarding the Twenty-One Demands on China were published. Therefore, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs has expressed great dissatisfaction with this breach of international trust and has commissioned Dr. Hayashi Ikuo, a prominent authority on Japanese diplomatic issues, former President of Keio University, and a member of the Imperial Academy, to draft a lengthy rebuttal essay. It is scheduled to be published in mid-October to reject the harmful biases against Japanese-American diplomacy. After being conveyed this intention by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the doctor, despite being 79 years old, gladly agreed for the sake of Japanese diplomacy. With the assistance of the authorities, he extensively researched the diplomatic materials of China, Japan, and the United States at that time. From the free and impartial standpoint of a scholar, he refuted Lansing's arbitrary and fallacious views, stating that the Japanese-German war was based on the Anglo-Japanese alliance, with the goal of world peace, and based on facts such as the spirit of friendship with China. The full text reaches 80 pages of the original manuscript and is titled "Lansing's Memoirs and Its Slanders." It is decided that the essay will be published in the diplomatic magazine "Gaikō Jihō" in mid-October. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will translate it into English to make the world recognize Japan's just position. (Domei, 23rd)

League of Nations Financial Report Advocates Adjustments to World Prices

(London) The League of Nations Financial Committee issued a report today stating that because there is no parity between prices and currency values, exchange rates cannot be balanced. This is a major obstacle to the progress of global recovery. The report agrees with the views of the Economic Committee, that is, if we want to restore economic exchanges to normalcy, we must eliminate the abnormal gaps that separate the price levels of various countries. The report also fully agrees with the opinion that it is now appropriate for countries to handle currency issues themselves and that holding a world conference at this time would not be beneficial. Any attempt at international economic cooperation should first focus on the opinions of a limited number of countries that seem to have influence over current events. Furthermore, it believes that future currency adjustments, if not accompanied by the relaxation of strict import restrictions, and ultimately leading to their elimination, will not bring any progress to the current economic situation. (Reuters, 23rd)

(London) Financial figures here explained that this report advocates that countries in the Gold Bloc should adjust the price of their currencies so that they are equivalent to the currencies of the Sterling Bloc. Regarding this matter, when French Treasury personnel visited Washington earlier, the U.S. government is rumored to have provided a promise to maintain the current exchange rate between the U.S. dollar and the franc. However, financial figures here do not want to maintain the exchange rate between the pound and the franc. Therefore, the negotiations currently being conducted by Britain, France, and Belgium are of great significance. (Havas, 23rd)

Moscow: Red Army Exercises; 2,000 Paratroopers Participate

(Moscow) Yesterday, the Moscow Military District held tactical exercises. 2,200 paratroopers parachuted behind "enemy" lines. Subsequently, a large number of aircraft transported 3,000 soldiers over 420 kilometers, landing and joining the paratroopers. They launched effective actions behind "enemy" lines. Those who came to review included Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars Molotov, People's Commissar of Defense Voroshilov, and Marshals Tukhachevsky and Yegorov. (TASS, 23rd)

Japanese Finance: Requests 3.3 Billion Yen; Income 2.7 Billion Yen

(Tokyo) The total amount of the budget requests from various ministries for the next fiscal year has reached 3.3 billion yen. The Ministry of Finance is currently reviewing its contents. The Ministry of Finance intends to decide on the budget amount approved for each ministry based on the revenue from the planned increase in national taxes. According to the results of the cabinet meeting on the 22nd, the new revenue for the next fiscal year includes an increase of 200 million yen in tax revenue, 30 million yen in higher tariffs, 30 million yen in profits from increased tobacco prices, 70 million yen in increased revenue from various other sources, and 70 million yen in funds transferred from special accounts of the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications, totaling 400 million yen. In addition, there is a total of 1.6 billion yen in various revenues, including last year's ordinary revenue and temporary ordinary revenue. The sum of the two is about 2 billion yen in ordinary revenue excluding public bonds. The amount of public bonds issued is about 700 million yen. Therefore, the total revenue for the next fiscal year is 2.7 billion yen. The Ministry of Finance will have to cut 600 million yen from the 3.3 billion yen budget requested by the various ministries. (Domei, 23rd)

Insurance Fees Provided for Japanese Goods Transported to China

(Tokyo) The Japan Marine & Fire Insurance Association held an emergency meeting on the 22nd to discuss the issue of raising insurance fees for goods transported to China. The results of the decision are as follows:

(1) Goods transported to Shanghai: 1% for maritime transport, 5% for warehousing on land.

(2) Goods transported to the Yangtze River area (excluding Shanghai): only 0.5% for maritime transport, 10% for warehousing on land.

(3) Other areas south of the Yangtze River (excluding Shanghai, Macau, and Hong Kong): only 0.25% for maritime transport, 10% for warehousing on land.

It was decided to implement this on ships setting sail from the 24th. (Domei, 23rd)

British Expeditionary Force Lands in Haifa; Atmosphere of Wartime; Arrested Arabs Sentenced

Haifa. The first batch of the British Expeditionary Force to Palestine, departing from Britain, landed here at dawn today. The wharf area suddenly took on a wartime atmosphere. So far, 1,400 people have arrived from Aldershot, including some administrative staff. Large quantities of military supplies and war materiel are now being continuously shipped in by cargo ships. Camps, canteens for soldiers, and field hospitals are currently being built in the suburbs of this town, which will be used as the expeditionary force's base. (Reuters, 23rd)

Jerusalem. Today, according to an official announcement, since the start of the Arab general strike in Palestine, a total of 2,643 Arabs and 346 Jews have been arrested. Among them, 1,646 Arabs and 218 Jews have been sentenced. Another 710 Arabs and 71 Jews have been acquitted. Currently, 287 Arabs and 71 Jews are still under trial. (Reuters, 23rd)

Indian Council of States Advocates Reducing League of Nations Dues; Government Opposes Withdrawal from the League

Simla. The Indian Council of States today passed a motion advocating a reduction in India's contribution to the League of Nations expenses by a vote of 35 to 6. Although the Indian government expressed its support for the above motion, it was quite opposed to the motion proposing India's withdrawal from the League of Nations, so it did not vote on it. (Reuters, 22nd)

Air Race Between London and South Africa; Departure Set for Next Tuesday; Amy Johnson Prepares to Participate

Liverpool. The famous British female aviator, Mrs. Mollison, is currently trying to join the Schlesinger Air Race from London to Johannesburg, South Africa, which will take off from Portsmouth next Tuesday. The aircraft Mrs. Mollison will use will be the "Miss Liverpool," the same aircraft that the famous British aviator, Mr. Black, crashed and died in at the airfield here last Saturday. This air race was initiated by the South African industrialist Mr. Schlesinger, from Portsmouth to Johannesburg's Palmiet Kuil Aerodrome, a total distance of 6,500 miles, and must be completed within 120 hours. The winner will receive a prize of £4,000. (Reuters, 23rd)

Des Moines, Iowa, USA. Republican presidential candidate Landon gave a campaign speech here today, for the first time appealing to farmers in the Midwest for support. He said that if elected president, he would like to fulfill all outstanding obligations of the government to farmers and briefly outlined his program for permanent agricultural revitalization. Subsidies will be provided for cotton, wheat, tobacco, and other agricultural products that are exported and consumed in the United States. He also promised to pay full attention to crop insurance, amend the Federal Warehouse Act so that farmers can use their harvests as collateral to borrow money from the government, and store their harvests. Measures to Restrict Official Telegram Fees

(Nanjing) Since the implementation of the strict enforcement of the revised official military telegram fee and restriction measures by the Ministry of Communications, the following sixteen provinces that have agreed to pay fees in accordance with regulations include Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Henan, Hubei, Hunan, Shandong, Fujian, Sichuan, Jiangxi, Suiyuan, Gansu Qinghai, Yunnan, Guizhou, etc., as well as the Northwest Bandit Suppression Headquarters. A few other agencies still state that they have financial difficulties and cannot comply. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications has drafted measures and presented them to the Executive Yuan for instructions, consulting with the Ministries of Finance and Military Affairs to determine the following three measures, requesting the Executive Yuan to forward them to the National Government for compliance, and sending a letter to the Central Secretariat for review. (1) Various agencies sending telegrams, starting from July 1, should uniformly pay in cash in accordance with the above revised measures. All military agencies that fail to comply should be ordered to be responsible for payment. If other agencies are unable to pay due to the fact that the budget for the 25th year has already been allocated and the amount listed for telegram fees is insufficient, they should state the reasons and report to their respective supervising agencies for review. (2) Telecommunications is an important national undertaking. If it is not thoroughly rectified, its impact on politics and military affairs will be significant. Rectification and maintenance require funds everywhere. If the measures are not strictly followed, there is a risk of collapse. Various agencies must comply with the stipulated measures, and those who do not comply may have their telegram services suspended. (3) Non-urgent matters should be sent by express mail instead of sending telegrams at every turn. Telegram texts should be concise. The Executive Yuan has recently issued an order to comply. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

(Special Dispatch, 23rd)

Jiangsu Province Holds Air Defense Exhibition

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Air Defense Exhibition held a grand opening ceremony at the Zhenjiang Provincial Public Stadium on the 23rd, attended by more than 10,000 people. The ceremony was very grand. Chairman Yu Jingtang reported on the preparations and the great significance of the air defense exhibition. Guan Lisheng, Chen Tao, and others then gave speeches. The ceremony ended at 10:00 AM. Afterwards, the propaganda team lined up and paraded, and divided into groups to carry out propaganda. At the same time, the Nanjing Air Force General Station sent three aircraft to Zhenjiang, soaring in the sky and performing various stunts, and dropping various colored propaganda items. The six exhibition halls of the People's Education Museum displayed no less than two or three thousand items. The models included those controlled by electric current, and the activities were vivid. Personnel were on the scene to explain, which aroused the interest of the general public. Therefore, 50,000 people visited the exhibition. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Estimates of the Yield of Major Winter Crops

(Nanjing) The China Agricultural and Industrial Research Institute has now released the final estimated figures for the yield of major winter crops in various provinces this year as follows: Wheat 461,555,000 shi, Barley 162,748,000 shi, Peas 69,096,000 shi, Broad Beans 62,253,000 shi, Rapeseed 49,572,000 shi, Oats 18,036,000 shi. Compared with the yield of various winter crops last year, wheat increased by 35,503,000 shi, barley increased by 4,672,000 shi, peas increased by 2,195,000 shi, broad beans increased by 1,189,000 shi, rapeseed decreased by 177,000 shi, and oats increased by 592,000 shi. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Improving Saline-Alkali Land in Changlu; Trial Planting of Cotton and Wheat

(Tianjin) The Changlu Alkali Land Improvement Committee raised 50,000 yuan to improve 100,000 mu of alkali land in Beicang, south of Tianjin. First, the Yongding River was requested to be silted to change the soil quality and wash away the alkalinity. Then, aid was provided to the households to try planting cotton and wheat. This year, the Alkali Land Improvement Committee spent a total of 55,290 yuan on cotton goods and 19,380 yuan on well-drilling loans. The cotton planted yielded 90%, and the soil improvement has been effective. (Special Dispatch, 23rd)

I Will Not Participate in the Brazilian Exhibition

(Nanjing) The Brazilian Embassy sent a note to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs requesting that we participate in the International Commodity Sample Exhibition. After consideration by the Ministry of Industry, it was decided not to participate, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs responded to the Brazilian Ambassador. (Special Dispatch, 23rd)

The Central Disciplinary Committee Announces Disciplinary Cases

(Nanjing) The Central Disciplinary Committee announced five disciplinary cases: (1) Zhang Zanxun, Magistrate of Huai'an County, Jiangsu, was penalized for violating the law, with a 10% reduction in monthly salary for a period of three months; (2) Pan Jiatian, former Magistrate of Lianshui County, Jiangsu, was penalized for negligence in allowing prisoners to escape, with a 10% reduction in monthly salary for a period of two months; (3) Xu Youchuan, Magistrate of Wujiang County, Jiangsu, was given two demerits for negligence in allowing prisoners to escape; (4) Wen Xingzhi, former Magistrate of Anxiang County, Hunan, was penalized for perverting the law and harming the people, engaging in debauchery and corruption, with a 10% reduction in monthly salary for a period of three months; (5) Wang Bocheng, Magistrate of Liling County, Hunan, was demoted one grade and reassigned for illegally abusing punishment. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Corrected Provisions for Civil Servant Aircraft Donation

(Nanjing) The Hunan Provincial Government found ambiguity in the first item of the Civil Servant Aircraft Donation Measures, which states that those with a salary of 30 yuan or less are exempt from donation, and those with a salary of 30 yuan or more to 50 yuan will voluntarily donate 2 jiao. They requested instructions from the Executive Yuan. To clarify the provisions, the Executive Yuan has changed the provisions of the first clause of the second item to: those with a salary of 30 yuan or less are exempt from donation, and those with a salary of 31 yuan to 50 yuan will donate 2 jiao per month. The order to comply has been issued. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Eurasia Aviation Corporation Insures Passengers

(Nanjing) In order to ensure the safety of passengers, Eurasia Aviation Corporation has signed an insurance contract with the German Allianz Insurance Company. The main compensation conditions are: (1) In the event of death due to an aircraft accident, the company will compensate 10,000 yuan; (2) In the event of complete disability due to injury, the company will also compensate 10,000 yuan; (3) In the event of complete loss of work ability due to injury, the company will inspect the degree of injury and death and compensate for medical expenses on a daily basis, with a maximum amount of 10 yuan per day. This insurance does not require passengers to pay a separate insurance fee; all expenses are paid by Eurasia from the ticket price to the insurance company. In the event of an accident, after the compensation is determined, Eurasia will also pay it to the passengers, without any direct relationship with the insurance company, and without any procedures. It is understood that these insurance measures have been implemented this month. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Shanxi Grain Prices Soar

(Taiyuan) Grain prices in the southern part of this province are soaring. Wheat prices are around 20 yuan per shi, twice the price at the time of this year's new wheat harvest. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Gu Zhutong Recruits Talents Back Home

(Guiyang) Gu Zhutong, Chairman of Guizhou Province, stated that because this province has previously experienced political changes many times, many talents from all sides, due to different political views, have taken refuge in other provinces. He has issued an order hoping that all will return to their hometown and await their ability to be used. He also ordered the commissioners and magistrates to properly protect these personnel. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Yu Hanmou Prohibits Gambling by Staff

(Guangzhou) Yu Hanmou ordered all staff members and their families to strictly prohibit gambling on the 23rd, and violators will be severely punished. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

(Guangzhou) The authorities of the British Concession in Shameen, Guangdong, responded to the Guangdong Provincial Government's ban on gambling and promulgated new anti-gambling regulations. After 11:00 PM, without a permit, free entry and exit are prohibited. The Guangdong Provincial Government today promulgated 14 articles of the detailed rules for the implementation of the Provisional Regulations on Prohibition of Gambling. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Central Bank Establishes Shantou Branch

(Guangzhou) The Guangdong Branch of the Central Bank has decided to establish a Shantou Branch. On the 23rd, Liu Wangsu was appointed as the director of the Shantou Branch preparation office. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Gold and Silver

London gold price today was 137 shillings and 2 pence per ounce, down 2 pence.

London silver market was stable today; spot and futures each fell 0.0625, to 19 pence and 4375. Indian selling, speculators buying, trading was small.

Mount Lyell silver market opened following London, falling 5 pounds sterling. The December futures opened at 44.45, 44.82.

Exchange Rates

Anglo-American: The London foreign exchange market was quiet but active this morning. The Anglo-American exchange rate opened at 5 dollars and 7 and 125/1000 cents, up 0.0625 from yesterday's American closing. It fell 0.0625 an hour later, and then fell another 0.125 at 1 p.m., to 5 dollars and 6 and 9375/10000 cents. The Anglo-French exchange rate opened up 1 pound sterling to 77.03. It fell back 5 pounds at 11 a.m., to 76.98, with no further changes.

Cotton and Wheat
