Zhou Yuji and His Wife

— Zheng Kanzi

—The Ming Dynasty was overthrown by valiant generals and their wives, like Zhou Yuji and his wife—

Over three hundred years ago, during the waning years of the Ming Dynasty, a retired seventy-year-old Vice Commander of the Embroidered Uniform Guard in Jinzhou Garrison was bedridden. He had been paralyzed on one side for three years. His situation was dire. His position was hereditary; he inherited it at the age of seven when his father died, becoming a Vice Commander of the Embroidered Uniform Guard. In his prime, he followed Yang Hao in managing affairs in Korea (in 1597, the 25th year of the reign of Emperor Wanli of the Ming Dynasty), and was promoted to Commander of the Embroidered Uniform Guard for his military merits. In his later years, he offended the eunuch Wei Zhongxian and was demoted to his original position. After retirement, his son, Yuji, should have inherited the position, but he only had this one son and no other relatives. Yuji was unwilling to leave home, preferring to give up the position to stay and care for his elderly father. However, this old Mr. Zhou had always been generous in helping others and had not saved any money for his retirement. Now, they relied entirely on Yuji's hunting for a living. Going into the mountains to hunt required at least a day and a half. The patient was bedridden, needing tea and water and constant attention. Therefore, Yuji would not go hunting unless the rice and firewood were completely exhausted and he had no other choice. Sometimes, he would be fully armed, going to the back of the house to lead his horse, but peering through a hole in the wall, he would see his father's unwell expression. Unable to leave, he would rather endure hunger. Other times, he would be halfway there, hearing his father's moans from afar (obviously a psychological effect), feeling deeply distressed and immediately reining in his horse and galloping back. As for his father, he was also unusually concerned about his son. Yuji's face was naturally round, but old Mr. Zhou always felt that his son was getting thinner by the day. Everyone who knew Yuji respected him, but old Mr. Zhou always worried that his son would be bullied. As soon as Yuji excused himself to go out, the moment the door moved, he would think his son had returned. When Yuji went hunting, if the weather showed any sign of change, he would pray with tears in his eyes, waiting until his son returned before stopping.

One day, Yuji went out hunting, and before long, the sky suddenly turned completely yellow. Old Mr. Zhou guessed that a strong wind was coming, or it would rain, and he was both afraid and worried, constantly muttering to himself, "Son, there will be a big wind and rain soon, come back!" After waiting for a while without seeing his son return, he changed his words and said, "Heavenly Lord, let the wind and rain come another day; for the sake of the people, don't let my son suffer."

In fact, old Mr. Zhou was overthinking everything. Yuji had undergone rigorous training since childhood and was now very strong and robust, able to draw a bow with hundreds of pounds of force as easily as if it were nothing. He had high ambitions and was very capable of enduring hardship; he would not consider wading through fire and water to be anything, let alone a little wind and rain. He remembered that four years ago, Yuji was a guerrilla officer in the capital garrison. At that time, most of the officers in the capital garrison were descendants of meritorious officials and eunuchs, accustomed to extravagance and licentiousness. Seeing Yuji's diligence, frugality, and kindness, they looked down on him. Yuji not only did not mind but instead advised them, "You are all pampered youths, how can you withstand a great enemy? Why not practice martial arts when there is nothing to do, for future use, so as not to waste the country's salary." Hearing Yuji's words, they laughed at him for being pedantic. Yuji ignored them and diligently practiced martial arts, so everyone else fell into depravity, while he became physically strong and vigorous. This time, Yuji decided to prepare provisions for his father for one or two months. Fearing that he would ruin his plan, he dared not think about the current difficulty of separation, only thinking that for one or two months, father and son could stay together, never leaving each other's side. Just as Yuji was chasing rabbits and deer in the mountains, a distinguished guest suddenly arrived at his home. This guest, surnamed Liu, was a current General. When he was still unsuccessful, he often stayed at the Zhou family and received many kindnesses from old Mr. Zhou. To repay his gratitude, he had promised his beloved daughter, Bingniang, to Yuji in marriage. Later, he became successful while the Zhou family declined, and he intended to break off the engagement. Old Mr. Zhou also felt that "marriage should be between equals," and never mentioned the marriage, planning to agree as soon as General Liu opened his mouth to cancel the engagement. Unexpectedly, General Liu looked down on this prospective in-law and even wanted to directly marry Bingniang to someone else, without going through the formalities of canceling the engagement with the Zhou family. Fortunately, Bingniang's heart was set on Yuji and she refused to break the engagement, arguing forcefully with her father. Originally, Bingniang had lived with Yuji since childhood, and Yuji taught her all the martial arts he learned from his instructors. They had made vows of eternal love, saying that in the future they would become husband and wife and sacrifice themselves together to serve the country. General Liu could not bear his daughter's righteous rebuke, and also because his daughter was too capable to control, he had to agree to recruit Yuji to join the General's mansion. He was now personally visiting for this matter. Old Mr. Zhou felt that Yuji would eventually marry a wife, and since General Liu was unwilling to break off the engagement, he had no choice but to let Yuji join the family. Before the matter was settled, the wind suddenly began to blow strongly, and old Mr. Zhou was worried about Yuji, unable to talk vigorously. General Liu thought that his prospective in-law was intentionally treating him coldly and was about to leave, using the excuse of coaxing Bingniang. Just as he was about to bid farewell, Yuji returned. That day, he had only caught half a hunt, because he saw the sky becoming increasingly terrible in the mountains, remembered that the windows at home were not closed properly, and feared that his father would suffer, so he had to come back early.

General Liu had left the Zhou family when Yuji was seventeen years old, and it had been eight years since then. Seeing that Yuji had grown even more handsome and heroic, he could not help but respect and love him. So he sat down again and explained his intentions to Yuji. Yuji stood in front of General Liu, cupping his hands and listening respectfully. After listening, he looked at his father without saying a word. Old Mr. Zhou understood that his son meant to let him decide. He felt that for Yuji's future, he had to agree, so he said to General Liu, "Brother, is there anything else you haven't considered for Yuji? I believe in you, I agree with you, you choose a good day and take Yuji to join your family."

Yuji originally observed propriety and did not express his opinion. He did not expect his father to not immediately agree to General Liu's request. At this point, he could not help but speak. He turned to his father and said, "Father, Uncle Liu knows that you are old and sick and that I alone cannot take care of you properly, so he is sending his beloved daughter to help me. I am extremely grateful for this. As for asking me to leave you to become his son-in-law, I would rather die than obey. Uncle Liu is a reasonable person, and I don't think he would do such a thing." His voice was very loud, and every word was clear to General Liu. General Liu dared not mention anything else, only saying that he would go home to discuss it further before making a decision.

A few days after General Liu returned, he sent someone to bring Bingniang over. From then on, the Zhou and Liu families rarely interacted. It is said that when General Liu returned home, he wanted to break off the engagement again. Bingniang argued with him for several days. He became angry and sent Bingniang to the Zhou family, declaring that he would no longer care about her.

After Bingniang arrived at the Zhou family, the Zhou family immediately prospered. Hunting outside and caring for her father-in-law at home, the couple took turns. In addition to hunting, they also engaged in animal husbandry. In less than two years, they had a thousand sheep. Unfortunately, old Mr. Zhou contracted this symptom and could not enjoy it for long. In the third year after his daughter-in-law entered the door, all his functions ceased to work, and he died peacefully in his son's arms.

After old Mr. Zhou died, the Manchus often invaded, becoming increasingly severe, and Jinzhou could no longer be a peaceful place to live. One day, Bingniang said to Yuji, "The country is being invaded by foreigners, now is the time for heroes to die on the battlefield. Why don't you join the army immediately? I think my father definitely needs people there. Go ahead! Don't worry about me being here alone. I can go back to my parents' home. Love for one's flesh and blood is innate, my father won't refuse to take me in. If you don't want to break up our family, I am willing to stay here. I often go hunting in the mountains and have met twenty Mongol women. They are all skilled in riding and archery, and extremely brave. I have become friends with them for life and death. I plan to bring them over to live with me as soon as you leave, and practice martial arts with them every day. When you are in a position to be independent and have the authority to recruit us, we will definitely come and join your command to serve the country. Who says women can't save the country? Who says women can't charge into battle? We want to break historical records and set a good example for future generations." Bingniang spoke with great decisiveness and force, her eyebrows showing an inviolable aura.

Yuji was very moved by Bingniang's words. Just then, a maid brought tea in. Yuji took the teacup, without thinking, smashed it on the ground with a bang, splashing碎磁黃水 everywhere. The maid was startled, and Bingniang quickly waved her hand to tell her to leave. Yuji turned around and knelt in front of Bingniang, pointing to the ground and saying to her, "How about I swear with you to shatter my body and spill my brains on the ground to repay the country?" Bingniang quickly returned the bow and said, "This is exactly my wish."

Yuji slowly helped Bingniang up and sighed to her, "Ah! You are brave, you are chivalrous, you are filial, you are loyal——" Suddenly, he changed his tone and said, "Sister, I believe you understand me. The reason I have accumulated wealth in recent years is not to 'ask for houses and seek fields,' but half to entertain my father in his old age and half to donate money to help the border. Now, unfortunately, my father is dead." He could not help but shed tears, "What is the use of keeping the property? Let's take it all and distribute it to supplement the military expenses! I used to hold a position in the capital garrison, so there is no need to go to my father-in-law's place. As for you, it's better to wait for me at home, so that you can often visit my father's grave when you have time. When I need your help, I will come in person or send someone to pick you up. Bring those twenty Mongol women to live with you, now is the time when the country needs talent, no one is useless. But you must remember, never neglect your archery skills. If you don't practice in peacetime, where will you have the skills to use in times of emergency?"

Bingniang agreed to everything. After a few days, after everything was arranged, Yuji went to the tomb to bid farewell to his father, left Jinzhou, and joined the army in the Pass. By the seventeenth year of Chongzhen, Yuji had been promoted several times for his accumulated military merits, already serving as the General guarding Shanxi and the three passes of Daizhou, and was awarded the title of Commander of the Central Military Governor's Office of the Crown Prince, naturally Bingniang and the Mongol women had come to serve in the army.

At that time, not only were the border guards in emergency, but also the rebel bandits in the Central Plains were rampant beyond description. Shaanxi and Shanxi had already fallen, and the capital region was collapsing. Only the Ningwu Pass, guarded by Yuji and his wife, stood firm like a pillar in the middle of the stream. Seeing that the news was too urgent, Yuji immediately increased the number of locked soldiers by two thousand, under the command of Xiong Tong. When the troops arrived at the riverbank, the rebellious general Chen Shangzhi welcomed the bandits and forced Xiong Tong to return to the town and say that Yuji had surrendered. Yuji angrily scolded, "I have received great kindness from the country, how can I follow you rebels? You lead two thousand soldiers, unable to stop the bandits, and instead come here as a spokesman for the bandits?" Then he ordered, "Execute Xiong Tong immediately." After Xiong Tong was executed, Yuji sent the chief of the sentinel office, Yang Zhirong, to take the head to the capital and request reinforcements.

On the fifteenth day of the second month, the rebel bandit Li Zicheng led hundreds of thousands of troops directly to Ningwu Pass. Zicheng, since breaking through Taiyuan, had come sweeping through victoriously, full of pride. He said to his subordinates nonchalantly, "Ningwu Pass is neither strong nor dangerous, and its military strength is weak. To break through it is simply like crushing dry weeds. You pass on my decree, saying, 'If Ningwu Pass is not taken in five days, a great massacre will be carried out.'"

Yuji had just taken over guarding Ningwu Pass, and everything had to be rearranged, which was time-consuming and laborious. Moreover, this pass had always lacked military preparation. Yuji trained his troops day and night, selecting only a few thousand brave men from the city. Compared with the bandit army, we were few and they were many, truly a case of a mantis trying to stop a chariot. Yuji knew that the capital would definitely not send reinforcements, and even if they did, they would not be able to arrive in time. He was very anxious and could not help but show his worry on his face. Seeing this, Bingniang was afraid that it would delay the military plan, and secretly comforted Yuji, "In times of danger, composure is essential for success. Have plans for victory and plans for defeat, do your best and leave the rest to fate. There is nothing for us to worry about."

"Then what are you planning?" Yuji asked, still with a worried look.

"Planning to be a general who dies fighting to the end. Your oath to 'shatter your body and spill your brains on the ground' can truly be put into practice today." She spoke with great strength and composure, which truly gave Yuji a lot of encouragement and comfort. Yuji happily said, "Just like you said, I have also made up my mind."

Yuji then summoned his troops, inspiring them with loyalty and righteousness. The couple led the soldiers themselves, and before the bandits had settled their camps, they charged out, directly attacking the core of the bandits, killing many of the bandit army's elite. But because the bandits were many, their momentum was only blunted but not broken. After more than a dozen battles, the bandits had already approached the city. Yuji and his wife tried their best to defend, firing cannons and killing more than ten thousand bandits. Yuji's battle plan was to deploy troops outside the city during the day, using battle as defense; at night, he withdrew the troops into the city, climbing the walls to attack. By the third day, the gunpowder was exhausted. An officer said to Yuji, "The bandits' power is too great, why not negotiate a truce with them?" Yuji replied, "We have only fought for three days and have already killed more than ten thousand bandits, what are you still afraid of? If we are lucky enough to win, none of the army will lose their righteousness; if we are unfortunate enough to lose, you can hand me over to the bandits and everything will be fine." After Yuji finished speaking, he opened the door and fought bravely, killing several thousand bandits.

At night, the bandits thought that both sides were exhausted from fighting and everyone needed to rest, so nothing would happen, and they were not prepared at all. Unexpectedly, in the middle of the night, Yuji and his wife led hundreds of brave men, climbing down the city walls and directly breaking into the bandit camp to kill bandits. The bandits were startled, and one of the bandits, who did not have time to put on armor or saddle his horse, was already separated from his head and body. At that time, the ones who killed the most bandits were the twenty Mongol women, a fresh force. The bandit soldiers, in the firelight, saw the women wearing silver armor, holding bright long knives, running quickly and silently, and were shocked by their power. Before they could guard against it, a cold light flashed, and they suddenly felt a sharp pain, not realizing that their head blood had already been splattered on their bodies. Originally, the Mongol women in Yuji's command were paid like assistant generals. Yuji selected twenty strong men with outstanding martial arts skills and had each of them marry a Mongol woman. They were not used in battle unless it was absolutely necessary. They received full training and rest, so they were able to kill countless enemies.

This raid on the camp defeated the bandit army, and they were afraid and retreated twenty miles at night. At this time, the city had already run out of arrows and food, barely managing to hold out for another half a month, and reinforcements still did not arrive. Yuji had no choice but to decide to fight to the death. So he first ambushed brave soldiers everywhere and opened the door to pretend to surrender. Zicheng knew that the defending soldiers had no way out but to surrender, so he believed it and sent more than ten thousand bandit soldiers into the city. As soon as the bandit soldiers entered the city, Yuji immediately lowered the city gate, and with the sound of a signal cannon, the ambushed soldiers rose up and killed the bandit soldiers, leaving not a single piece of armor. Four brave generals of the bandit army were also seriously injured.

Zicheng, having suffered repeated defeats, was extremely frustrated. He believed that Ningwu Pass could not be broken and feared that if they continued to hold out, the entire army would be wiped out, and he intended to flee back to his old nest. Someone in the bandit army came up with a plan for Zicheng, "Your Majesty has hundreds of thousands of troops and cannot defeat a few thousand people, how can you command the world? Now the elite of the city have been exhausted, and there are not many old and weak left. Why not take the city at this time? We are many and they are few, and if we can distinguish between the main and guest armies during battle, attacking one with ten, there is no reason not to win. Your Majesty can use a surprise victory, and order the soldiers to take off their hats as a mark, and kill those who are wearing hats." Zicheng listened to his words and attacked with all his troops. Yuji's soldiers, some of whom could fight ten people alone, some of whom could fight hundreds of people alone, were so disparate in strength that they were still able to hold out for four days and nights. When the city was breached, the residents, grateful for the loyalty and righteousness of Yuji and his wife, risked their lives to cooperate with the remaining soldiers, engaging the bandits in close combat, street battles, and resistance. Therefore, the entire city's people died heroically together, and not a single child or woman was willing to surrender. Yuji led the citizens in street battles, jumping and fighting on foot. When his spear broke and his sword broke, he could still kill dozens of people with his hands. Yuji was eventually seriously injured and captured alive by the bandits. Yuji cursed the bandits incessantly. The bandits tied him to a high pole and shot him to death with random arrows, his entire body covered with arrows like a hedgehog. Afterward, the bandit soldiers were moved by Yuji's loyalty and bravery, and many people shed tears for him.

While the street battles were raging, Bingniang led the women to climb onto the roofs, resisting to the death. Each of their arrows could kill a person, never missing. The bandit soldiers dared not approach and set fire to the houses, but they did not come down, standing and letting the fire burn them to death. At the same time, the twenty Mongol women, on the other hand, launched a surprise attack. They hid in the house, opening all the inner and outer doors, and tying Yuji's steed to the front door. The bandit soldiers were very afraid of Yuji and originally dared not enter, but wanting to risk getting this steed, everyone rushed to pull it. The women inside fired crossbows in succession, shooting to death several hundred people. When the arrows were all shot, they jumped into the fire one by one.

Zicheng's attack on Ningwu Pass was a victory on the surface, but in reality, the losses were truly great. He inspected the troops and found that the generals and soldiers killed before and after numbered nearly one hundred thousand, and most of the remaining ones were disabled and weak. He wanted to raise and replenish his troops here, but looking at the city he had obtained, not a single person remained, not a single斗 of grain was stored, not a single usable weapon, not a single piece of cloth that could be clothed, the houses were either completely destroyed or half-collapsed, and the four walls were一片瓦礫, simply like a ruins. Seeing this situation, Zicheng constantly shook his head and sighed, "Such a victory is no better than defeat. If I had known this, I would not have come to attack Ningwu Pass. This Yuji is truly formidable! Alas! It is also destined that we are unlucky, why didn't we use a counter-espionage scheme first, and only attack after we had lured the tiger away from the mountain?" He swallowed a mouthful of saliva in regret and said, "We originally planned to go straight to the imperial capital, but who dares to think so now? There are one hundred thousand soldiers in Datong, one hundred thousand soldiers in Xuanfu, one hundred thousand soldiers in Juyong, and a total of two hundred thousand soldiers in Yanghe and other towns. If they are all like Ningwu Pass, would there be anyone left of us? It is better to return to Shaanxi, and wait for the troops to rest and expand before finding another auspicious road." The bandit generals all nodded in agreement and decided to return to Shaanxi tomorrow. So the bandit generals gathered around to discuss how to make the wounded and sick soldiers retreat slowly. They talked late into the night, when suddenly it was reported that Jiang Huai, the General of Datong, had sent someone to submit a letter of surrender. The bandits were very surprised and happy, and hurriedly set up a banquet to treat him with great care. Just as they were seated, it was reported that Wang Chengyun, the General of Yifu, had also sent a letter of surrender, and had sent one hundred riders to welcome them. Zicheng was overjoyed beyond expectation and immediately changed from retreating to advancing, using the various rebel generals as the vanguard, and advanced straight to the capital, forcing Emperor Sizong of the Great Ming to his death.

The bandit soldiers who arrived at the capital, some with half faces and some with broken hands and feet, were all wounded during the battle at Ningwu Pass. They told people, biting their fingers, "General Zhou is truly a hero, if there were another town like Ningwu, how could we have come here? It is rare that his wife is also as virtuous and loyal as he is." The prestige of Yuji and his wife quickly spread throughout the capital, and no one who talked about them was not amazed and awed, calling them大人 and 夫人.

Publishing Industry

From "The Analects" to "Lost Classics"

— Yi Fu

—The Gradual Decline of Humorous Essays—

Since Mr. Lin Yutang advocated humorous essays and published the semi-monthly journal "The Analects," in recent years, a humorous atmosphere has permeated the surroundings, as if enveloping the entire China in the atmosphere of humor and late Ming essays.

"The Analects" started by promoting humor and advocating the late Ming essays. Consequently, this humor, that humor, humorous writing, humorous conversations, even advertisements in movie theaters and various stores, all regarded humor as orthodox and labeled it as modern. Humor's popularity truly reached its peak.

At that time, bookstore publishers also leaned towards this path. As a result, Yuan Zhonglang suddenly rose to prominence again. You punctuate, I proofread, and some even achieved fame because of this.

Lin Yutang's advocacy of humor led to the popularity of late Ming essays, and even led to the surge of heavily discounted books. Many bookstore owners and Hai Pai (Shanghai School) literati who set up stalls relied on this for a living. This is probably something that Mr. Lin Yutang, the giant who advocated humor as the orthodox, did not expect.

Whether humorous works have value is a matter of public opinion. I believe that "highly serious" works and "sweet stabs" of gentle mockery, allowing people to feel like they want to cry but cannot, want to laugh but cannot, is another style of literature. Sima Qian's "Biographies of Jesters," which says, "Their subtle and pointed words could resolve disputes," is originally not blameworthy, and we even welcome it warmly.

But how easy is it? To create a humorous work that is just right is an extremely difficult task. As a result, attempting to draw a tiger but failing and resembling a dog instead, leads to the production of boring and low-grade works. This causes people to become irresponsible, taking pleasure in making frivolous jokes, with one person starting it and a hundred following suit, using precious time for meaningless work. "Purity" and "leisure" may lead to national demise.

But we must investigate where this humor originated and why it suddenly surged. This is also due to the relationship with the era's environment. The Jin people were not born fond of pure conversation, nor did they like to renounce the world. Because there was no way out in the environment, they had no choice but to use wind, moon, poetry, and wine to kill time. Present-day China is indeed an extremely dangerous era. Being Chinese does not mean that everyone is a bloodless man. Those with blood and energy cannot express themselves properly, so a portion of people without the courage to overcome the environment turn to humor and jest. This is also not surprising. In Mr. Xu Yu's open letter to Mr. Zhu Guangqian, I feel that a few sentences are fair, and it is worth transcribing them as follows:

"I also believe that the most sound ideal is multifaceted development, but I do not oppose a person's private preferences. At the same time, in cultural history, we often know that there are sometimes fads and popular things. Observing this phenomenon with an objective attitude also has a necessary background. Speaking coldly, the periodicity of these waves is also very interesting. People like Yuan Zhonglang were suppressed in the Qing Dynasty, and it is normal for them to raise their heads now. Soon it will naturally calm down to a suitable listed price. I don't know what to use to explain this phenomenon. Perhaps it is a kind of property? Or perhaps it is the evolution of the dialectical thesis, antithesis, and synthesis. In short, this kind of thing has a necessary waxing and waning, and naturally human power can promote its early birth,

and can also promote its early death. …

The rise of humor and the raising of Yuan Zhonglang's head are originally ordinary things, but it is unnecessary for them to become a trend. Moreover, because of imitation and vulgarity, the drawbacks are not few. Mr. Zhu Guangqian explained this very thoroughly. In his open letter to Mr. Xu Yu, there is the following explanation:

"I have the same feeling about the late Ming essays. It itself is very fresh, but after many people imitate it, it becomes a kind of gentle tone. I have always believed that in art, a person has his own unique insights. If he does not have his own unique insights and specializes in imitating someone else's unique style, it is okay to do this as an exercise in childhood, but if he treats it as a serious career, then it seems unnecessary."

I believe that Mr. Zhu Guangqian's open letter is the most sincere in pointing out the meaninglessness of the humor school and the unnecessity of advocating late Ming essays.

Following the publication of "The Analects," there were also "Ren Jian Shi" and "Cosmic Wind." "Ren Jian Shi" and "Cosmic Wind" can be said to be sister publications of "Shen Yu" ("The Analects"). "The Analects" has been published for 83 issues, with a history of three and a half years. The trend of humor has lasted for so long, which must be considered the effort of Mr. Yutang and others. "The Analects" was initially edited by Lin Yutang and Tao Kangde. Later, because he developed "Ren Jian Shi," Yutang handed it over to his assistant Kangde to edit.

"Ren Jian Shi" was edited by Lin Yutang as the editor-in-chief, and Xu Yu and Tao Kangde as editors. However, after 42 issues, for some reason with Liangyou Book Company, it finally did not continue to be published.

From the 83rd issue of "The Analects," Tao Kangde withdrew, and Yu Dafu and Shao Xunmei edited it. Now, the orthodox direct line only retains "Cosmic Wind." (To be continued)

Confucius

— Du Xiu

Compiled by Tong Xingbai, one of the "Junior High School Student's Literature Series," published by Zhonghua Book Company.

Blind worship and blind opposition are equally eternal sinners in academics. Regarding Confucius, he has been blindly worshiped by people for thousands of years, but he has also been unreasonably attacked and cursed by people. Those who worship him rarely conduct detailed research on Confucius's doctrines, and those who attack them are even more unwilling to understand Confucius's doctrines rationally. As a result, in today's Chinese society, the following phenomenon has been created regarding Confucius: those who oppose Confucius scold those who revere Confucius as restorationists, reversing the course of thought; those who revere Confucius scold those who oppose Confucius as extremists, poisoned by thought. Such people who criticize blindly without seeking thorough understanding, whether they revere Confucius or oppose Confucius, are not only sinners against Confucius but also moths in the academic world!

Therefore, no matter which great thinker, great politician, or great educator's doctrines we study, we have absolutely no reason to criticize them arbitrarily unless we thoroughly research their thoughts and doctrines before making a judgment. Otherwise, this criticism is definitely not genuine criticism but blind abuse.

Confucius is a great politician, great educator, and great thinker who has been unanimously recognized in China for thousands of years. However, there are simply no specialized books that thoroughly research and systematically discuss Confucius's sayings. We cannot consider this a big joke. Moreover, it is not just a joke, it is simply a great shame in the Chinese academic world!

Mr. Tong Xingbai compiled a book entitled "Confucius" in the "Junior High School Student's Literature Series" published by Zhonghua Book Company. Although it is only a separate volume of about 50,000 words, it has already made precise and careful descriptions of Confucius's life and the content of his doctrines. We cannot but recognize this as a matter worthy of joy.

In this thin booklet, we only need to look at the compilation and classification of its chapters to understand its breadth and depth. The first part is "Confucius's Life and Environment." In this part, Confucius's family background, childhood, adulthood, and old age are discussed without omission. What is particularly noteworthy is that the historical background, political background, social background, and ideological background of Confucius's time are also analyzed one by one. This scientific research method is already worthy of our attention, and the detailed and profound analysis makes us unable to avoid reading it. The second part is "Confucius's Philosophical Thought," which is the most important part. Most people who study Confucius's philosophical part often focus on Confucius's philosophy of life, political philosophy, and educational philosophy, etc., and mostly omit the details of Confucius's philosophical method. The reason for this phenomenon, of course, is that the part of Confucius's philosophical method is really too difficult. In fact, if we do not understand Confucius's philosophical method, we cannot accept the most profound part of this great thinker's learning and conduct, and we cannot be considered to understand Confucius or study Confucius's doctrines. The book specifically elaborates on the "Confucius's Philosophical Methods" item, detailing the principles of Confucius's philosophical methods of consistency, adaptability, the mean, rectification of names, and the measuring square. This point should be given serious attention. The third part is "Confucius's Immortal Career," which specifically lists Confucius's political achievements, literary achievements, and educational achievements. This part, when read in conjunction with Confucius's life history, can give us a clearer understanding of Confucius. The fourth part is "The Great Confucius." The content of this part is entirely about the profound and lasting influence of Confucius on later generations, whether in political or social aspects. Therefore, if we can carefully read this single volume, those who have a deep understanding of Confucius can benefit from mutual comparison and research; those who have no knowledge of Confucius can gain a general outline of Confucius.

The author believes that the most admirable point of the book is that the argument is very objective and there is no stubborn prejudice at all. This is, of course, the fundamental condition for studying all academics, but in the attitude of today's Chinese people in studying Confucius, it is a treasure that is lacking. The author hopes that junior high school students, college students, adults who revere Confucius, and progressive elements who oppose Confucius will all come and read this "Confucius" to know that blind worship and blind opposition are equally eternal sinners in academics.

The book is published by Zhonghua Book Company, with a real price of 50 cents, beautifully printed on Taoling paper, with a total of 180 pages and 50,000 words.

Supplement to the Shanghai News

Talk

"Asianization Flowing Westward!"

— Wu Ci

"Asianization Flowing Westward!"

Writing these four words out of nowhere might strike the reader as odd. But it’s not really out of nowhere: three female artists, in order to "promote our country's beautification (not culture)," applied to the Ministry of Education for subsidies, which have now been approved. With approval granted, they could have packed their bags and set out to "promote" it. However, it’s said that the petition, “written in balanced prose, with excellent emotion and rhetoric,” needed to be published. After reading it, I’m now excerpting a few passages here to express my admiration:

"Humbly considering that we lack the talent of Xie Daoyun, but are aware of the global intersection of the world, and can promote the progress of the art world, European customs have long permeated eastward, so Asianization can naturally flow westward, adhering to the orthodoxy of the original sect, and creating a fixed view of European and American eclecticism, fearing the inability to bear the burden of countless lost threads, and hoping for the greatness of the future with small youth... returning home upon successful completion, repaying the kindness of parents with the heart of an inch of grass, taking up the pen to travel abroad at this time, receiving the benevolence of the sweet pear tree..."

Reading this entire "emotionally and rhetorically" powerful article from beginning to end, it is indeed sonorous and affecting, with the sense of lingering for three days. However, whether it is "lacking the talent of Xie Daoyun," "valuing the global intersection," or "small youth," only this "Asianization can naturally flow westward" requires considerable deliberation.

Why is that?

What should be considered first here is what "Asianization" is. If "Asianization" is an abbreviation for "Asian culture," it seems that Chinese culture this time is undoubtedly representing Asia. Regardless of whether others acknowledge it, we should also look in the mirror. What exactly is modern Chinese culture besides ancient times? If there is nothing, then how can this "Westward Flow" flow? If "Asianization" is not regarded as "Asian culture" but only as "Asianize," such as "concretize," "clarify," etc., this word "ize" has the meaning of a verb, then it means to make Westerners become "Asianized" or "Asianized into Chinese," telling them to abandon airplanes and ships and instead ride Chinese sailboats and ox carts, telling them to abandon electric lights and running water and instead light truly Chinese-style "oil lamps," and draw water from ancient wells: telling them not to send wireless telegrams or watch movies, but to use Chinese "messengers" and watch local operas in ancestral halls: telling them to grow their hair and wear a braid, telling them to take off their high heels and bind their six-inch round feet into three-inch golden lotuses.

To be honest, modern Chinese culture is no longer domestic. We should admit our lack of progress and humbly accept it, perhaps being able to "catch up." If we still hold on to the prejudices of "barbarians" and "Chinese," thinking that Chinese culture developed the earliest, and that no matter how much others progress, it is not worth mentioning, ultimately, it will inevitably lead to cultural disintegration and then stop.

Taking art as an example, I don't know what Chinese painting has that is worth "officially promoting" abroad, or what can represent "Asianization" and "flow westward"? The mountains, rocks, thatched cottages, water buffaloes, herdsboys, flowers, and plants painted by the ancients hundreds of years ago are still the same set in the hands of modern people, and they also arrogantly inscribe things like "imitating the brushstrokes of the Song and Yuan dynasties," making foreigners think that China is still stuck in the 15th and 16th centuries, an era that knew nothing about the world, that China is a backward country, and that the Chinese nation is the least progressive nation.

Page 20

This is simply "showing ugliness" rather than "promoting."

Since it is "small youth" and the "future is great," then humbly study abroad, "promoting" I think there is no need to bother, and "Westward Flow" is absolutely not allowed to "flow."

Village Chief

— Shi Xi

In my memory, the two people who left the deepest impression on me are Wang Zicheng and Wang Baodong.

Wang Zicheng was a man in his thirties, thin and tall, about four feet tall, often wearing a long white-grey bamboo cloth shirt, and always wearing double-strand straw sandals on his feet (woven from thread and bamboo hemp). Regardless of sunny or rainy days, it was always those straw sandals. Only at the end of the lunar year would you see him change them.

In the village, he was the commander of the militia team, and he carried himself with great authority. However, he treated my mother like family. He and Wang Baodong were mortal enemies. Why? He couldn't say it himself, but when speaking to my mother, he would start cursing angrily!

"Damn it, that piece of dog crap Wang Baodong should just be called Wang Jindeng." Then, he would recount his crimes in an indignant voice: "His heart is blacker than coal. He embezzles at least half of the public funds before handing them over to the district office, yet he claims to be selfless. He doesn't do any work all day. Otherwise, where did he get the money to build that big house and buy that leather coat?..."

After venting his anger enough, he would carefully warn:

"Old lady, these words should only be known to you and me, don't say them out loud. I have no grievances or hatred with him, Wang Baodong..."

Wang Baodong, like Wang Zicheng, often came to our house to talk to my mother and clear his name. In secret, although he didn't know what bad things Wang Zicheng was saying about him, he was afraid that he would take away his position as village chief. He always had a smile on his face when he spoke, and always addressed my mother as "old lady, old lady." Sometimes he would call out angrily for no reason:

"Wang Zicheng, that dog-hearted man, I don't know how many private buns he's sold, and he's involved in smuggling salt and cattle (evading customs duties). Sometimes he goes out at night with those men from the militia team (called Zhuang Ding Dui in Sichuan), supposedly to stand guard, but secretly they go to "catch night snails" and rob those wealthy farmers and small landlords..."

Sometimes they would meet in our house, both with smiles on their faces, exchanging pleasantries and being as polite as brothers. My mother often said that they were just temporarily upset and that they would be fine after a few days.

But behind their backs, they would say bad things about each other, pounding their chests and recounting the other's sins.

One day, we were sending my mother back to the city, and were talking excitedly about a small matter when we suddenly heard a shout from behind. Looking back, we saw Wang Baodong, who was also going to the city. He shouted loudly:

"Old lady, why don't you take a sedan chair? How are those sedan carriers supposed to make a living?" He then said in a low voice, "That dog-hearted Wang Zicheng caused trouble again last night. Does he think I don't know that cattle smugglers are leading cattle past the edge of his dam?"

After saying this, he smiled and left.

Not far away, we ran into Wang Zicheng, who was hurrying from another village, his face looking very bad. He angrily complained:

"Wang Jindeng, that bastard, is saying bad things about me outside. Old lady, if you hear anything, please don't believe him."

At eight o'clock in the evening, everyone had just finished dinner, and the farmhands were washing their hands and feet in preparation for going to bed. Uncle Tai'an, who smoked opium, was lying in bed puffing smoke, and we were all gathered around him. On the field road, a kerosene lamp illuminated our front gate wall. Someone said softly: "Wang Baodong is back..."

But before long, we heard a cry for help flying over from afar. Everyone was shocked. The farmhands, awakened from their sleep, grabbed their tools and rushed out, even Uncle Tai'an, who smoked opium, dropped his opium pipe and ran to see.

Wang Baodong was lying in a pool of blood, already unconscious. In the distance, Wang Zicheng also led several militiamen rushing over. He was shouting for people to carry the body away, while sobbing and saying to the crowd:

"My fellow villagers, our Wang Baodong has been assassinated. This is a misfortune for our village, and also a misfortune for me, because I have lost a powerful assistant..."

As he spoke, tears dripped from his eyes. Everyone shook their heads and said that Wang Zicheng was a good man.

Soon he was elected as the village chief.

Scenic Area

— Hu Weixiong

On the second day after returning to my hometown, several close friends took the first bus to my house. My hometown has a high historical status. Recently, after the highway opened, it's easy to travel back and forth from Shanghai in one day. Even this small county town often has wealthy old men coming to patronize it, just like other scenic areas.

Due to my job, I rarely have a few days to return to my hometown each year, and every time I come and go quickly. When the rickshaw pulls through the streets, I only feel that the shops in my hometown have learned the set of Shanghai's big sales, building colored archways, hiring drummers, and I can't see any other reason why this county town has become a scenic area.

But my friends have such a request, they want me to guide them on a tour. This is really a difficult problem for me. I left my hometown to study in middle school and it has been ten years. Even if my hometown has any scenic spots, I should also be the one being guided. So I always refuse:

Page 21

Shanghai Postal Administration Mailing Schedule

All branches in Shanghai can send registered express airmail and handle remittances, savings and other matters

Page 22

Page 23

"Don't I know? It's just that rich people have nowhere to spend their money, so they think of this small county town!"

But they never give up. This time, because I had something to do and returned to my hometown, they immediately came as a group. I immediately found my cousin to come over, he naturally knows more than me. In the morning, we toured the streets for a week, and what we saw were big sales, colored archways, and the same economic downturn everywhere as in other county towns. I wanted to use this reason to hope they would take the afternoon bus back to Shanghai with me, but they asked my cousin to go with them to visit the ×× Garden, the Confucian Temple, the school grounds, and even thought of going to the nearby × Mountain × Peak for a fun outing. These scenic areas have long been blurred in my memory, they memorized them as fluently as if they were locals. As the host, I couldn't refuse at this time. Guided by my cousin, we first went to ×× Garden after lunch.

×× Garden is a private garden in my hometown. When my grandfather was alive, I had been there once, but I can't remember what the garden looked like now. The rickshaw pulled through a small street that could only pass one car body, and then it was all in winding alleys. I almost suspected that our car had left this small county town. How could a local not have been to this place? After circling through another narrow street, we finally saw one of the plaques of ×× Garden hanging in front of a temple-style gate, gold letters on a black background, shining brightly in the sunlight. It seemed to have been hung up recently, right?

Walking through the second house, it was really like a temple, quiet and without a single person. Turning the corridor, there was a moon gate with "Curved Path Leads to Seclusion" written on it, and only then did we hear noisy sounds inside. I was thinking back to whether this was the place when I came with my grandfather, we had already arrived at the four-sided hall. There is a lotus pond in front of the hall. This pond is still in my mind, I once ate two lotus seeds from this pond. Now the lotus leaves have all withered and yellowed, and there are still a few green leaves floating on the water, but they are so small that the so-called listening to the sound of rain on the remaining lotus is useless for such small leaves, and besides, it floats on the water, the rain on it is the same as falling into the pond.

The four sides seem to have been recently repaired, with plaques, screen strips, and low tables, with a few small round tables and wicker chairs set up in the center, prepared for tourists to come here to taste tea and enjoy the lotus. Now although there are no lotus flowers to admire, and there is a sign posted on the side door saying "Residential Area Inside, No Entry for Tourists," the scenic ×× Garden has already been fully viewed, and naturally we have to sit down and rest.

"How is it?" I started asking my friends.

"Don't give up until you reach the Yellow River." One of them answered me: "It's always more elegant than drinking tea at the Deyilou."

Everyone smiled slightly, looking disappointed.

There are many tourists, and there are also Western teachers, because that day was Sunday, and there are probably many who came in their own cars.

We each brewed a pot of tea, and they all wanted to leave before sitting for even ten minutes. However, the opinions were not consistent. Some wanted to see the Confucian Temple and school grounds again, and some also agreed with me to take the 3:30 bus back to Shanghai.

My cousin paid the tea man one dollar, and that honest countryman said with a smiling face that he wanted another dollar. There were five of us in total, and five pots of tea cost two dollars. I said with a smile:

"Isn't this the price of a dance hall?"

"Today is Sunday, please give me a little extra reward," the tea man said with a smile again.

My cousin waved his hand at him. "We are all locals, don't try to fleece us, one dollar is already being polite."

Hearing my cousin's local dialect, he thanked us and walked away.

"Alright." As we stepped out of the gate of ×× Garden, I said to them; "It's not that rich people have nowhere to spend their money, that's why they come here to be fools!"

Young Master... Man Fu

Mid-Autumn Moon

Yes, the "Mid-Autumn Moon" is particularly bright. The wealthy are celebrating wildly under this extraordinarily bright Mid-Autumn Moon night, drinking wine, dancing, singing, and leisurely telling and listening to "anecdotes of Emperor Tang Ming." But this is only a festival for the wealthy to enjoy!

But what about us poor people? This extraordinarily bright moonlight cannot shine into our pigeon-cage-like thatched or low houses. What's in the thatched and low houses are: emaciated faces eroded by hunger; crying children with empty stomachs; sick people groaning in bed with no money for medicine; fierce eyes of debt collectors at the door; forcing people to go to their deaths!

The Yue Zilin family was driven to the path of destruction. - When the "Mid-Autumn Moon" was particularly bright.

Yue Zilin used to have a fortune of about 100,000, but after a series of attacks, he was unable to keep this fortune and went bankrupt and fell into poverty. However, the lifestyle habits of a fortune of 100,000 made it impossible for him to change his stubbornness even in his fallen state. He was desperate to save face, and he was unwilling to let his second daughter - A Rong (i.e., younger sister) become a maid; but the food for a family of six was heavily burdening her older sister - the eldest daughter, and it was impossible to support them by working.

A Rong is an innocent little girl, but because she is beautiful, she is deceived by the young master of the landlord, Hu Xinmei.

Knowing that this is a deception. It is exactly: "He is tired of playing with those young ladies, and now he wants to make fun of us poor people!"

"You are still young, you won't understand, but you must know that even if they really like you, they will forget you in a few days..." Her older sister is right. Her older sister is a new woman, she is doing the women's liberation movement and negotiating with the masters to improve their treatment. Therefore, the factory where they work is on strike. But for the sake of life, her younger sister was deceived and abandoned, and their mother suffered heavy blows. First, her mother harmed her three or four younger sisters, and then she committed suicide herself.

The younger sister ran out madly. What about the older sister? She is leading the masses to resist those cruel masters!

The father could not catch up with them and returned in disappointment. "Why are you living alone?" Alas! All dead.

In short, such things are happening layer by layer in the city; however, those children are innocent. It's too cruel!

Save the children!

Movie News

Two Blockbuster Films Soon to be Released at the Grand Theater

(1) Frontier Heroic Legend

American Paramount Pictures, this spring, had "Battlefield Heroes" released in Shanghai, which caused a great sensation at the time, perhaps everyone still remembers it. Now, they have produced another film of similar nature. The film is the latest work of the great director Victor, in collaboration with Fred MacMurray. The film features Indians launching sudden attacks, massive sieges with giant stones and poisoned arrows, the intensity of the battles, and the strangeness of the war preparations are even more than in "Battlefield Heroes," it is indeed a work worth appreciating in the new autumn cinema scene, it is said.

"Passionate Village Teacher"

Playing at the Great Shanghai

(2) Anthony Adverse

Anthony Adverse is an immortal masterpiece by the great American writer Hervey Allen, which has been translated into a dozen other languages. Warner Brothers of America has now adapted it for the screen. When the company was producing this film, they were very cautious, using all their energy in terms of both money and talent, and it took two years to complete. The director is Mervyn LeRoy, and the leading actors are Fredric March and Olivia de Havilland. After its release, it shocked the entire film industry, and everyone said that it was not only Warner Brothers' best production of the year, but also a miracle of Hollywood. It is now reported that the film has been shipped to Shanghai, and it has been scheduled to be screened at the Grand Theater from 9:15 PM on the first day of last month (Thursday), it is said.

New Publication Introduction

"Coffee" Bi-monthly Magazine, edited by Chen Yaoting, is dedicated to carrying exciting news from the film, dance, and singing industries, as well as urban features, humorous sketches, strange customs communications from various places, interesting cartoons, and photos of famous film, dance, and singing stars. The two-color edition opposite is a new type of publication that encompasses everything with both pictures and text. It is now available for sale at the Sima Company newsstands at a price of one dime per issue.

"Venus" Monthly, which has now published six issues, was founded in Tianjin by the Wang Bolong and Cilong brothers in conjunction with well-known figures in the literary and artistic circles of Pingjin, with the aim of promoting culture and stimulating literary and artistic interests, and also with drama, film, comics, bronzes and stone inscriptions, calligraphy and painting as supplementary content. Each issue is available in Shanghai, and major bookstores and newsstands in the city are selling it for only fifteen cents per issue. The printing is slightly better, and all pages are printed on heavy-weight woodfree paper. It is also planned to increase the size of the next issue, and contributions are welcome. The local correspondence address is Wang Cilong, c/o No. 7 Zhouye Lane, Fulv Road, French Concession.

The famous Swedish comic strip "Alfie Atkins" is the world's leading humorous continuous comic. There are translated versions in English, American, Japanese, Italian, French, German, and other countries, which is enough to prove that "Alfie Atkins" is recognized by people from all over the world as the world's number one humorist. With its humor that can relieve worries, its implicit and extremely satirical nature, the clarity of its lines, and the novelty of its composition, it is especially rare among the world's continuous comics. The cartoonist Zhang Guangfei has now compiled and selected sixty works from his thousands of famous works, none of which have ever been published in any Chinese magazines or newspapers. The content almost encompasses the starting phenomena of China. The opposite side is printed in five colors, exquisite and eye-catching, and the binding conforms to modern art. The book is issued and published by Dazhong Books Publishing House, No. 1 Xuexi Street, Ximenwen, Shanghai, and direct mail orders and wholesale are welcome from outside the city. Each batch is sold for only twenty cents in national currency. All cars, localities, major bookstores, and newsstands are selling it, it is said.
